  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1466c43c-a48e-4d33-91a4-39df28805e7a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText3089808637130624449" style="display:none"><b>WHAT IF YOU REALIZED THE TERRIFYING BOOK YOU WERE READING WAS ALL ABOUT YOU?</b><br /><br />A BRILLIANTLY CONCEIVED, DEEPLY DISTURBING PSYCHOLOGICAL THRILLER ABOUT A WOMAN HAUNTED BY SECRETS - AND THE PRICE SHE WILL PAY FOR CONCEALING THE TRUTH<br /><br />When a mysterious novel appears at Catherine Ravenscroft's bedside, she is curious. She has no idea who might have sent her <i>The Perfect Stranger</i> - or how it ended up on her nightstand. At first, she is intrigued by the suspenseful story that unfolds.<br /><br />And then she realizes.<br /><br />This isn't fiction.<br /><br /><i>The Perfect Stranger</i> recreates in vivid, unmistakable detail the day Catherine became hostage to a dark secret, a secret that only one other person knew - and that person is dead.<br /><br />Now that the past Catherine so desperately wants to forget is catching up with her, her world is falling apart. Plunged into a living nightmare, she knows that her only hope is to confront what really happened on that terrible day... even if the shocking truth might destroy her.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_23615087').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_23615087').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_23615087').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

<span id="freeTextContainer11477312369035557121">If you trust me at all, then trust me on this one. Take a chance and read it. <br/><br/><u>Disclaimer</u> It took me awhile to get into this. I had almost given up, but then‚Ä¶<br/><br/>From the reviews I‚Äôm reading I liked <u>Disclaimer</u> more than some. <br/><br/><b>The Hook</b> - The blurb - <i>‚ÄùWhat if you realized the terrifying book you were reading was all about you?‚Äù</i> Come on now, isn‚Äôt that enough to reel you in?<br/><br/><b>The Line</b> ‚Äì <i>‚ÄùAll I felt was soft filth, and it got into my skin and under my fingernails, and its stink invaded my nostrils, clingin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11477312369035557121" style="display:none">If you trust me at all, then trust me on this one. Take a chance and read it. <br /><br /><u>Disclaimer</u> It took me awhile to get into this. I had almost given up, but then‚Ä¶<br /><br />From the reviews I‚Äôm reading I liked <u>Disclaimer</u> more than some. <br /><br /><b>The Hook</b> - The blurb - <i>‚ÄùWhat if you realized the terrifying book you were reading was all about you?‚Äù</i> Come on now, isn‚Äôt that enough to reel you in?<br /><br /><b>The Line</b> ‚Äì <i>‚ÄùAll I felt was soft filth, and it got into my skin and under my fingernails, and its stink invaded my nostrils, clinging to the hairs, soaking up into the tiny blood vessels and polluting my entire system.</i><br /><br /><b>The Sinker</b> ‚Äì Catherine Ravenscroft soon realizes the book she finds by her beside is far more sinister than a light work of fiction. She‚Äôs intrigued by this suspenseful story <u>The Perfect Stranger</u> until she realizes it‚Äôs all about her. Where did it come from? Who wrote it? And why was it left for her? It threatens to expose a secret from her past, one she thought hidden for all time, the consequences which could topple her very existence.<br /><br />Ren√™e Knight plotted this psychological tale with precision. A satisfying read with questions we all struggle to answer. How well do we know our spouses? How strong is love? How well do we know our children? Would we lie for them? Do we see them as others do? Do we put them first, even before our spouses? What do we see but deny? Do we want to know the truth? Who do we trust? <br /><br /><u>Disclaimer</u> is about two marriages, two families, two boys, two sons. It is thought provoking. It‚Äôs a book within a book, its pages filled with revenge, betrayal, love, guilt, bravery, sadness, and brimming with human emotion. I thought I would scream if someone compared it to <u>Gone Girl</u> but they already have. Be warned this is no copycat. Knight earns the excitement that her debut deserves. <br /><br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/73431206-richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24824392-disclaimer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73431206-richard?shelf=thrillers-uk">thrillers-uk</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351169561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12920179488622410658">With a couple of reservations, I found Disclaimer by Ren√©e Knight to be well written, engrossing and quite chilling.<br/>Catherine, a documentary film maker is given a book. She is extremely disturbed to find that the book‚Äôs leading character is herself!<br/>Many years ago a terrible incident occurred - an incident that Catherine has never come to terms with, has buried and tried to erase. The book brings the poison flooding back and threatens to destroy her.<br/>The story is told mainly through two viewpoints</span>
  <span id="freeText12920179488622410658" style="display:none">With a couple of reservations, I found Disclaimer by Ren√©e Knight to be well written, engrossing and quite chilling.<br />Catherine, a documentary film maker is given a book. She is extremely disturbed to find that the book‚Äôs leading character is herself!<br />Many years ago a terrible incident occurred - an incident that Catherine has never come to terms with, has buried and tried to erase. The book brings the poison flooding back and threatens to destroy her.<br />The story is told mainly through two viewpoints, which works well and the tension builds effectively. It‚Äôs a tale of betrayal, obsession and growing paranoia.<br />There‚Äôs also a sadness that seeps through the narrative.<br />My only issue with the book was with a specific narrative device. <br />Psychological thriller writers often build a clever artifice, an arrangement of selective facts that create an assumed reality ....... a reality that comes tumbling down the minute a new fact or perspective is added i.e. a big surprise for the reader!<br />With Disclaimer however, it‚Äôs a little different.<br />In the first half of the novel especially, you are very aware that secrets are being kept from you, names are purposely omitted, events are deliberately jumbled chronologically and who said what is disguised. There is so much open misdirection and obvious omission that it almost feels like a taunt. At times intriguing, at times irritating!<br />But, even with this in mind ........... the inner lives and motivations of the main characters are well explored and I was always totally involved, gripped even. I looked forward to picking up this book to find out how things would end. <br />Hence the solid 4 star score. <br />A superior thriller in my humble opinion ......</span>
  <a data-text-id="12920179488622410658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1086639310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086639310" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086639310?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2015-release">2015-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=mystery-thriller-etc">mystery-thriller-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=first-novels">first-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086639310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12450744067948710960">I'm learning to be less bothered about hype. I've said over and over again that most of the hyped and praised and 'hotly anticipated' books I've read this year have been thoroughly mediocre, and yet only recently has it occurred to me that <i>of course</i> they are: it's mediocre books that sell the most. Hype still gets to me, I easily get caught up in the must-read-this-first excitement, but I no longer expect it to actually mean a truly great book.<br/><br/><i>Disclaimer</i> is a classic case in point - a much-talke</span>
  <span id="freeText12450744067948710960" style="display:none">I'm learning to be less bothered about hype. I've said over and over again that most of the hyped and praised and 'hotly anticipated' books I've read this year have been thoroughly mediocre, and yet only recently has it occurred to me that <i>of course</i> they are: it's mediocre books that sell the most. Hype still gets to me, I easily get caught up in the must-read-this-first excitement, but I no longer expect it to actually mean a truly great book.<br /><br /><i>Disclaimer</i> is a classic case in point - a much-talked-about debut suspense novel that sparked a bidding war and is already set to be translated into 20+ languages; you know the drill. In alternate chapters, it tells the stories of forty-something film producer Catherine and retired teacher Stephen Brigstocke, starting with Catherine's discovery of a book - apparently left on her bedside table - which, she finds, is about a part of her life she's managed to keep secret for twenty years. Convinced the author's revenge tactic will tear her family apart, Catherine becomes obsessed with finding out who has written it, and why. But what is this oh-so-terrible secret? And how are Catherine and Stephen, who becomes more and more of a sinister figure as the plot progresses, linked?<br /><br />As happens so often with these novels, the 'secret', when it's revealed, appears at first to be mundane and really pretty ordinary compared to the desperate paranoia and fear that's come before it. But there is a twist, and that was something I hadn't expected (on the whole, this isn't really a twisty book, at least not in that manufactured multiple-cliffhanger way). Unfortunately, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it involves a rape scene - I really thought I was going to be able to make it through a crime/thriller novel without one, but yet again, no. However, I did feel that the issue was handled very well at the end; Stephen's acceptance of Catherine's story, the comparison Catherine makes between Robert's reaction to the 'affair' then the rape, and her decision thereafter <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The biggest fault with <i>Disclaimer</i> is just that it isn't particularly well-written. There are advantages to the plain language (especially the fact that it doesn't go into detail about unnecessary things - no lengthy descriptions of what people had for dinner or dropping of middle-class brand names), but overall it's a bit flat, and the punctuation is awful, although that's something I am assuming (but can't be sure) will be amended in the published version.<br /><br />However, the <i>story</i> really is extremely compelling. After the halfway mark, it becomes pretty much unputdownable. There is an unexpected elegance to the plot that makes it work it better than many similar books I've read. The character of Stephen, in particular, is realised and developed very well. Catherine remains rather distant, but I suppose this is intentional, to keep the reader guessing about whether she's supposed to be sympathetic or not.<br /><br />There was something I found curiously nostalgic about this book. I'm not sure if that was because it reminded me of something specific, or because it reminded me generally of a type of book I used to read when I was younger. When I was in my teens I went through a crime phase and read loads of Agatha Christie, then moved on to stuff like Minette Walters and Barbara Vine - this brought memories of those books back to me, even though I can hardly remember any of the titles of those I read. <i>Disclaimer</i> will no doubt be marketed as a psychological thriller, but it doesn't have a lot of the typical characteristics of that genre as it's now understood. It is more of a suspenseful mystery, and if you take away the references to modern technology, the story could just as easily be set 50 or 60 years ago as in the present day.<br /><br />Does <i>Disclaimer</i> justify its hype? In terms of the audience it's meant to attract, the answer is probably yes. It's gripping, tightly plotted and emotive, the type of story that will have people on the edge of their seats/staying up all night/recommending it to everyone at work, etc. Still, there's something a bit empty and soulless about it, and I doubt it will prove to be very memorable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12450744067948710960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535758028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2727029987770891983">Another psychological thriller that's good enough, but not great.<br/><br/>I liked the unsettling premise of picking up a book in which your darkest secret is laid bare. For those of us who read a lot, it is exactly the kind of 'what if' that hits closest to home. I spend a lot of time wishing I was in certain books, but on reflection, am pretty happy i'm not, especially in the starring role. My turbulent past can stay there, thank you very much.<br/><br/>Beyond that, Knight does well with the trials and misunderst</span>
  <span id="freeText2727029987770891983" style="display:none">Another psychological thriller that's good enough, but not great.<br /><br />I liked the unsettling premise of picking up a book in which your darkest secret is laid bare. For those of us who read a lot, it is exactly the kind of 'what if' that hits closest to home. I spend a lot of time wishing I was in certain books, but on reflection, am pretty happy i'm not, especially in the starring role. My turbulent past can stay there, thank you very much.<br /><br />Beyond that, Knight does well with the trials and misunderstandings of family interaction, the relationships between people that are determined more by what is not known, or acknowledged, about others, than what is. It worked well in the denouement and was the basis for a relatively satisfying surprise.<br /><br />However, the novel had a light touch, and I was left unmoved. I felt no connection to any of the characters and little real interest in what happened to them. The book only took a few hours to read and as an easy distraction, it was fine. It won't be a story that I remember for long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2727029987770891983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7538342225204944054">This book surprised me in a good way. I'll admit I wasn't so sure in the beginning. I found the first 1/4 of this book a little confusing. Keep in mind that you will need to suspend your disbelief nearly throughout but if you can then it will make for a satisfying read if you like tricky psychological thrillers. And the ending, while maybe a bit over the top, was completely entertaining. This would make for an </span>
  <span id="freeText7538342225204944054" style="display:none">This book surprised me in a good way. I'll admit I wasn't so sure in the beginning. I found the first 1/4 of this book a little confusing. Once I was able to get into the flow of the novel it really did become a page turner. Keep in mind that you will need to suspend your disbelief nearly throughout but if you can then it will make for a satisfying read if you like tricky psychological thrillers. And the ending, while maybe a bit over the top, was completely entertaining. This would make for an excellent beach / vacation read.</span>

This story shows how the main character, Catherine, has a past that comes back to haunt her and destroy the life that she knows. I wavered between 4 and 5 Stars throughout.   <span id="freeText11260709496722891663" style="display:none">Disclaimer is a great debut novel! Not only is it a psychological thriller, but it is a thought provoking story about two families told from different points of view with really great character development! This story shows how the main character, Catherine, has a past that comes back to haunt her and destroy the life that she knows. I wavered between 4 and 5 Stars throughout. The very beginning, being a 4 because it took me a little while to get into the story, but once I caught on it became very good and had some twists that I didn't see coming that put it in the 5 range. The ending was a 4 for me. I will definitely be reading Renee Knights next book. Thank you to GR Friend Carol! If it wasn't for her review I probably would not have purchased this novel.<br /><br />Oh, it took me a week to read this book because I had a lot going on. It would have been much better if I had more time to dedicate to it. This book reads fast and would make a great beach read, rainy weekend or long flight read. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Smith" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith">Andrew Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1344834525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3447626940859274065">I've mentioned several times before that I'm not normally keen on stories set in ‚ÄòBlighty‚Äô - just too close to home. The settings remind me of work and the prevailing weather is normally dismal too. Two things that hit the wrong note for me from the get go. So the London setting of this debut novel from a former film documentary maker had ground to make up from the start. <br/><br/>However, it did kick off in interesting fashion with Catherine Ravenscroft (also a film documentary maker) finding a book bes</span>
  <span id="freeText3447626940859274065" style="display:none">I've mentioned several times before that I'm not normally keen on stories set in ‚ÄòBlighty‚Äô - just too close to home. The settings remind me of work and the prevailing weather is normally dismal too. Two things that hit the wrong note for me from the get go. So the London setting of this debut novel from a former film documentary maker had ground to make up from the start. <br /><br />However, it did kick off in interesting fashion with Catherine Ravenscroft (also a film documentary maker) finding a book beside her bed only to find it to be the story of a part of her own life she's desperate to forget! From this point the story is told, partly in flashback, both her her point of view and that of retired schoolteacher Stephen Brigstocke, who is introduced as a rather creepy character and whose relevance to the central narrative becomes apparent as we get deeper into the tale.<br /><br />In truth it is a well told story with several good twists and a decent cast of characters. It held my attention to a gripping denouement ‚Ä¶ and then unfortunately continued for a prolonged and unnecessary ‚Äòcleanup‚Äô. I'm not quite sure what came over the author at the end as all the last section does is to dilute what was already a satisfying mystery. The ending didn't quite spoil the book for me but is most definitely a case of less would have been more. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3447626940859274065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1283028320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283028320" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5143619-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546601194p2/5143619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283028320?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/5143619-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24824392-disclaimer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283028320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4000915202653731177"><i>A mother and her child on holidays in Spain. A young man in the same holiday resort, a terrible incident and misunderstanding that will tear two families apart.</i> <br/><br/>Catherine Ravenscroft has a seemingly happy life. Married to Robert, with a young adult son and a successful film-maker, she is content with how things are going. But when Catherine discovers an unfamiliar book at her bedside entitled, <i>The Perfect Stranger</i> she is shocked by what is written. The book will force her to relive an unspeakabl</span>
  <span id="freeText4000915202653731177" style="display:none"><i>A mother and her child on holidays in Spain. A young man in the same holiday resort, a terrible incident and misunderstanding that will tear two families apart.</i> <br /><br />Catherine Ravenscroft has a seemingly happy life. Married to Robert, with a young adult son and a successful film-maker, she is content with how things are going. But when Catherine discovers an unfamiliar book at her bedside entitled, <i>The Perfect Stranger</i> she is shocked by what is written. The book will force her to relive an unspeakable moment in her life from 20 years ago that she hoped would be forgotten forever. Catherine is desperate to find out not only how the book came into being in her house but also who wrote about something that supposedly only she and one other person who is now dead knew about.<br /><br />On the other side of the coin, we have Stephen Brigstocke who has had his world destroyed after the death of his young son Johnathon and wife, Nancy. After going through her belongings he will come across a manuscript that detail's a secret from a women he has never met, Catherine. Worse will come when he finds pictures taken by his son that will connect the two families and convince Stephen that his sons passing is because of this women. What will follow is a roller coaster ride of twists and turns as Catherine's life slowly implodes until the inevitable collision course when it is clear things are not as clear cut as they seem.<br /><br />As a self confessed fan of psychological thrillers i can honestly say this one can bat with the best of them. Combining beautiful and emotional writing with an intriguing storyline that will keep you guessing makes for an absorbing read. Throw in engaging characters in Catherine and Stephen, that you can't help but be drawn to with the sadness of there pasts and the tragedy that is the present they now encounter makes for a truly hard hitting family drama that will leave you thinking well after you have read the final page. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4000915202653731177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756455761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756455761" />
    <a title="Izzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy"><img alt="Izzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593145096p2/31211197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756455761?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Izzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Izzy" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy">Izzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062362278" href="/book/show/23015978-disclaimer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756455761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13238344839886974721"><b>DNFed @ 54%</b><br/><br/>The story is centered around a mysterious book the main character ‚Äî Catherine (I'd forgotten her name) ‚Äî finds in her home. Even though she doesn't remember buying it, she's just moved to a new place and figures it was probably something that'd gotten lost in the midst of her things before. She starts reading it, and horrified she discovers that the story is actually about a secret she thought would never see the light of day; a secret only she and someone dead for the past 20 years k</span>
  <span id="freeText13238344839886974721" style="display:none"><b>DNFed @ 54%</b><br /><br />The story is centered around a mysterious book the main character ‚Äî Catherine (I'd forgotten her name) ‚Äî finds in her home. Even though she doesn't remember buying it, she's just moved to a new place and figures it was probably something that'd gotten lost in the midst of her things before. She starts reading it, and horrified she discovers that the story is actually about a secret she thought would never see the light of day; a secret only she and someone dead for the past 20 years knew about.<br /><br />It's a very interesting premise, I'll give it that. But it falls short right at the first few pages. We have two perspectives, Catherine and a man, Stephen Brigstocke, a weird obssessive little man whose wife died a few years ago. At first it's not obvious how the two of them would be linked, but as Stephen's perspective advances ‚Äî it began two years before Catherine's ‚Äî the conections are made clear. I didn't click with the writing style right off the bat; Catherine's chapters were okay but Stephen's, told in first person, were pretty terrible. The writing was choppy and the metaphors were peculiar, to say the least:<br /><b>
  <blockquote>My hand, slippery yet firm, ejaculating the words as they flowed from Nancy into me.</blockquote>
</b><br />Ejaculating... the... words? Okay... that's not gross at all.<br /><br />And then there's the central conflict of the story, which is the secret hidden away in the pages of the mystery book and that is, supposedly, earth-shattering and utterly terrible.<br /><br />I found it stupid.<br /><br />So stupid, in fact, that I simply refused to believe that was it ‚Äî I could not believe that Catherine, who is theoretically a very strong, independent woman, a documentary filmmaker that goes after the big guys, would let her world fall apart because of something silly that could've been solved with a five minute conversation with her husband. So I got pretty annoyed and DNFed it, but I decided to skim to the end to see if there wasn't something I was missing.<br /><br />There was. And the twist made me even angrier. If you're curious as to what it is and doesn't want to read the book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Basically, the book tells the story of an alleged affair Catharine had twenty years ago with Stephen's son during a vacation in Spain, and the dude died saving her son from drowning. Pretty bad for her wedding, but she could've talked it out with her husband. But then there's the twist ‚Äî she never actually had an affair; the man raped her at knifepoint and made her take sensual pictures for him, and she went along with him because her son was asleep in the next room and she didn't want him to get hurt. After the dude dies (deciding for some mysterious reason to help the son of the woman he violently raped the night before) the police hand his parents his belongings, and in his camera his mom finds out the sexy pics he'd taken of Catherine, wrongly assuming they had an affair and he died trying to impress her. And then she writes the book telling the story from her "point of view", her husband finds it after her death and decides to torture Catherine with it because he's a horrible man, so on and so on.<br /><br />What I don't get is: Catherine was RAPED. I understand the guilt she'd feel at first but it's been twenty years, and after her husband receives the pictures Stephen's son had taken of her during that night and believes she was cheating on him, her marriage almost ENDED, all because she preferred to ler her husband think she was a cheater rather than someone who'd been raped? I honestly just. Don't. Get it. It makes no sense and she makes these stupid decisions simply to move the plot forward, which is annoying and shows the author didn't really have a story to begin with. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So yeah, I'm glad I didn't waste my time finishing this book. Terrible writing, terrible plot, terrible choices. You can read it for yourself if you'd like, because some people gave this really great reviews and maybe it just wasn't meant for my taste, but I wouldn't give it the time of the day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13238344839886974721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Barnsley" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley">Liz Barnsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=received-via-netgalley">received-via-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=top-crime">top-crime</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144779249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13553046213782292460">I loved this atmospheric, beautifully written novel, a real page turner and an intriguing and often twisty plot with some terrifically well drawn characters.<br/><br/>2015 is turning into another great year for books, most especially debuts and this one is definitely going to be somewhere near the top of the favourites list come the end of the year ‚Äì I was totally absorbed into the story and loved the emotion of it as much as the mystery element. A tale of two halves as we follow along with Catherine, who</span>
  <span id="freeText13553046213782292460" style="display:none">I loved this atmospheric, beautifully written novel, a real page turner and an intriguing and often twisty plot with some terrifically well drawn characters.<br /><br />2015 is turning into another great year for books, most especially debuts and this one is definitely going to be somewhere near the top of the favourites list come the end of the year ‚Äì I was totally absorbed into the story and loved the emotion of it as much as the mystery element. A tale of two halves as we follow along with Catherine, who mysteriously finds a book by her bedside, a seemingly fictional tale but one that hits very close to home. Opposite her is Stephen, a grieving husband who has his own story to tell. As things ebb and flow you are never sure who you should be sympathising with ‚Äì and there are many secrets to be revealed.<br /><br />I am a fan of a good psychological thriller and this hit that mark as well, plus there is a great family drama to be had here with some emotional and intense themes that drive the narrative in a most fascinating way ‚Äì I was utterly engaged with both Catherine and Stephen, their lives and their personal relationships and as it becomes obvious that not everything is clear cut, it is addictive stuff for sure.<br /><br />Definitely highly recommended ‚Äì a fuller review will appear upon release.<br /><br />Happy Reading Folks!</span>

  <span id="freeText14720400404191086228" style="display:none">Disclaimer doesn‚Äôt disappoint. It‚Äôs very cleverly written and will grip you, then surprise with unexpected twists. I was lost in this excellent thriller and couldn‚Äôt put it down.<br /><br />Catherine and Stephen have a good life and stable marriage, but all that is about to change. Their son Nicholas has recently moved out and although he hasn‚Äôt achieved all they hoped, he seems stable and happy in his work. It‚Äôs then that Catherine reads a book which mysteriously appears on the bedside of their new home. The book disclaimer has a neat red line through it ‚ÄòAny resemblance to persons living or dead‚Ä¶.‚Äô Catherine only appreciates the significance of this as she reads on!<br /><br />Catherine finds that she is the main character in the book and that it reveals a secret that she thought only she could now know. This is where it begins and we are off on a rollercoaster of a ride as Catherine‚Äôs world falls apart. I loved this psychological thriller as it played with my head as the story unfolded. I was never sure whose side I was on and not quite sure where my sympathy‚Äôs lay. <br /><br />I found the plot was well written and the story kept me hooked right to the end of the book. Disclaimer is a damn good thriller which I can thoroughly recommend.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300770498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12891124314433235688">Disclaimer: Results not typical. <br/><br/>Do I even need to say it? Apparently 2015 is to be the year that most popular books will fail to leave me wowed. Perhaps I'm reading too many within the same genre. Maybe I'm expecting too much. I suppose the why of it doesn't matter. What it amounts to is that my normal existence as a reader happily reading and loving the bestsellers is now marked by moments of self-doubt and slight bewilderment.<br/><br/>This book, Disclaimer, was okay. The pacing was too slow for my tas</span>
  <span id="freeText12891124314433235688" style="display:none">Disclaimer: Results not typical. <br /><br />Do I even need to say it? Apparently 2015 is to be the year that most popular books will fail to leave me wowed. Perhaps I'm reading too many within the same genre. Maybe I'm expecting too much. I suppose the why of it doesn't matter. What it amounts to is that my normal existence as a reader happily reading and loving the bestsellers is now marked by moments of self-doubt and slight bewilderment.<br /><br />This book, Disclaimer, was okay. The pacing was too slow for my taste but some of the characters were very well drawn, so that balanced it out. The protagonist was shrouded in mystery and her enemy was formidable, creepy and seemed to be unraveling before my eyes. I must admit that I did not see the end coming, which is a plus, however the very end was a little too implausible and without explanation. While it is receiving very high marks, I found Disclaimer to be forgettable. Maybe it's me?! 2.5 stars</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24824392-disclaimer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249404270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2484218997984732783">The hype surrounding this book's release has been insane, and the subsequent rave reviews seem to be everywhere, which makes me wonder - am I the only person in the world who was totally underwhelmed by this book? There have been lots of comparisons made to Gone Girl (and equally lots of people claiming that it's nothing like Gone Girl). I fall firmly into the former camp - this book IS like Gone Girl in the sense that I had absolutely no interest or sympathy for the characters whatsoever.<br/><br/>I've l</span>
  <span id="freeText2484218997984732783" style="display:none">The hype surrounding this book's release has been insane, and the subsequent rave reviews seem to be everywhere, which makes me wonder - am I the only person in the world who was totally underwhelmed by this book? There have been lots of comparisons made to Gone Girl (and equally lots of people claiming that it's nothing like Gone Girl). I fall firmly into the former camp - this book IS like Gone Girl in the sense that I had absolutely no interest or sympathy for the characters whatsoever.<br /><br />I've left it a few days between finishing the book and writing the review just in case my views change, but nope, after closing the book it left my mind totally, which personally I don't feel is the sign of a great story. <br /><br />The premise is excellent - who could fail to be intrigued by the idea of opening a book and the story being all about you? However, the premise was let down by a keep-you-in-the-dark plot and a series of shallow, weak and generally unlikeable characters. Ok, I admit, I don't like 'keep-you-in-the-dark' plots because I am generally rubbish at guessing what's going on. I'm the sort of person who needs movie plots explaining to me *as I'm watching them*. So this meant that I spent about half the book wondering what the hell was going on. This wasn't helped by the fact that the writing style was pretty clunky and the dialogue poor. <br /><br />It took some time before I felt interested enough in the story to actually *want* to read it rather than feel obliged to because I needed to do a NetGalley review. In fact, I was probably three-quarters of the way through before started enjoying it. But even then I kept getting thrown out of the story by awkwardly worded passages or odd dialogue.<br /><br />Overall, I was seriously disappointed by this book. The storyline was good, but the delivery poor. I never lost myself in this book, which is a shame. <br /><br />I was provided with a free e-copy of this book via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2484218997984732783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16666778463684835435">Catherine, a successful film-maker, is intrigued when she mysteriously receives a book entitled <i>The Perfect Stranger</i>. But as she reads the novel, she's horrified to read about a specific day in her <i>own</i> life--one that occurred 20 years earlier--which she's tried valiantly to forget. How could anyone know what happened that day? The only other person who truly knows is long dead. She's desperate to learn the identity of the author, and what he or she wants. <br/><br/>Intertwined with Catherine's narrative, </span>
  <span id="freeText16666778463684835435" style="display:none">Catherine, a successful film-maker, is intrigued when she mysteriously receives a book entitled <i>The Perfect Stranger</i>. But as she reads the novel, she's horrified to read about a specific day in her <i>own</i> life--one that occurred 20 years earlier--which she's tried valiantly to forget. How could anyone know what happened that day? The only other person who truly knows is long dead. She's desperate to learn the identity of the author, and what he or she wants. <br /><br />Intertwined with Catherine's narrative, is that of Stephen Brigstocke, a grieving widower, who has never met Catherine, but has discovered among his late wife's belongings, a manuscript detailing Catherine's most closely guarded secret, one she's hidden from her husband and son. This novel skillfully weaves alternating narratives (from past and present) and shows how one's horrific past can catch up and derail one's entire life.<br /><br />Mark Rubinstein</span>

  <span id="freeText3668857642536141106" style="display:none">DISCLAIMER is a truly engaging debut by Renee Knight, and a psychological thriller I will not soon forget. The story seems at first very simple, Catherine receives a book, which recounts a story she is all too familiar with - her own. As the story unfolds, we are told what happens through multiple POVs, which i always enjoy when it is done well, as it is here. It quickly becomes clear, that not all is as it seemed initially, and that the dubious book serves as the catalyst for some major revelations, and the ending definitely surprised me.<br />I read a fair amount of crime fiction, and this book really stood out as clever, original, while quite tragic as well. I look forward to whatever Knight comes up with next!<br /><br />Find more reviews and bookish fun at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.princessandpen.com">http://www.princessandpen.com</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135362490?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9430851513741974195">Catherine Ravenscroft is a person who seems to have an almost charmed life, when we first meet her in this novel. She is married to husband Robert and both of them have a successful and high status career ‚Äì Robert in law and Catherine in television documentaries. They have one grown son, Nicholas, who has not quite lived up the expectations they wanted for him; but he has moved out and is living an independent life. So, Catherine in 2013 is a respected and loved woman, who has recently moved hou</span>
  <span id="freeText9430851513741974195" style="display:none">Catherine Ravenscroft is a person who seems to have an almost charmed life, when we first meet her in this novel. She is married to husband Robert and both of them have a successful and high status career ‚Äì Robert in law and Catherine in television documentaries. They have one grown son, Nicholas, who has not quite lived up the expectations they wanted for him; but he has moved out and is living an independent life. So, Catherine in 2013 is a respected and loved woman, who has recently moved house and is looking forward to the future. However, a book seems to have appeared in her new home ‚Äì left seemingly in a pile by her bed, with the disclaimer, ‚Äúany resemblance to persons living or dead‚Ä¶‚Äù neatly crossed out with red ink.<br /><br />As Catherine reads the book, she realises that the main character is supposed to be her and that the story revolves around an incident which happened many years ago. Now Catherine is fearful of who knows the secret she has carefully guarded all these years. This thriller weaves an interesting storyline, revolving around Catherine and her family and Stephen Brigstocke; a retired teacher, who is determined to destroy Catherine‚Äôs life. It is difficult to review the book without revealing the plot and I have no wish to spoil your enjoyment of a thriller which is certain to be a big success in 2015. Catherine is a capable woman under attack, while Brigstocke is a creepy and insidious opponent. This has a lot of twists and turns, great characters and will keep you turning the pages until the end. A good debut and I look forward to reading more from this author.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11624792532402885192">At first I was frustrated with this book. I just wanted it to get to whatever it was that was at stake. Once it did, it was a really good read. A few parts dragged, and I found myself getting restless again, but then it picked back up, and during the last quarter of the book I couldn't put it down. <br/><br/>Definitely a psychological thriller, and one that will keep you guessing until the end. Though the reader will see some things coming, other things they won't, and that's what makes these types of rea</span>
  <span id="freeText11624792532402885192" style="display:none">At first I was frustrated with this book. I just wanted it to get to whatever it was that was at stake. Once it did, it was a really good read. A few parts dragged, and I found myself getting restless again, but then it picked back up, and during the last quarter of the book I couldn't put it down. <br /><br />Definitely a psychological thriller, and one that will keep you guessing until the end. Though the reader will see some things coming, other things they won't, and that's what makes these types of reads fun. Well, I use the word 'fun' loosely. This is a dark read, but anything less wouldn't do it justice. The author has a sharp grasp of the genre, and the reader feels all sorts of emotions. I'm glad this was a book club read for me. We'll have lots to discuss.</span>

<div id="review_1249543762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249543762" />
    <a title="Cleopatra  Pullen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3162627-cleopatra-pullen"><img alt="Cleopatra  Pullen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466403301p2/3162627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249543762?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cleopatra  Pullen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cleopatra  Pullen" href="/user/show/3162627-cleopatra-pullen">Cleopatra  Pullen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=favourite-2015">favourite-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249543762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16295159012910912139">I‚Äôm going to start this review with a bold statement ‚Äì this book will make my top ten reads of 2015. Yes it was so good that I can‚Äôt see me coming across ten other books that will beat this one.<br/><br/>So what‚Äôs it about? Well as with any book that depends on the reader not knowing very much before they start to appreciate the story, I can‚Äôt tell you very much! I can tell you that our chief protagonist, Catherine Ravenscroft has just moved house to a new apartment with her husband Robert when she comes </span>
  <span id="freeText16295159012910912139" style="display:none">I‚Äôm going to start this review with a bold statement ‚Äì this book will make my top ten reads of 2015. Yes it was so good that I can‚Äôt see me coming across ten other books that will beat this one.<br /><br />So what‚Äôs it about? Well as with any book that depends on the reader not knowing very much before they start to appreciate the story, I can‚Äôt tell you very much! I can tell you that our chief protagonist, Catherine Ravenscroft has just moved house to a new apartment with her husband Robert when she comes across a novel. Idly picking it up the book entitled Perfect Stranger with the standard disclaimer; any resemblance to persons living or dead scored through with red pen. She starts to read and to her horror she realises it is about her, and more specifically about a secret that she has kept for the last twenty years. All the reader knows at this stage is the secret involves her son Nicholas, their less than successful son, who at Catherine‚Äôs instigation has moved into a shared house in a bid to foster some independence and responsibility into his life. Of course the questions raised by the book are what is the secret? And just as importantly who knows and cares enough to write a book about it?<br /><br />Alternating with Catherine‚Äôs narrative we hear from another voice, that of a lonely old man, mourning the death of his wife, Nancy but at last determinedly clearing his house of her belongings, packing her clothes away and giving them to charity shops where he gets given cups of teas and a chance to talk about Nancy.<br /><br />The reason I enjoyed this book so much was the way that Renee Knight skilfully played on my emotions, changing my opinion of all of the characters who populate this book with an ease that left me reeling. My once certain opinion swept away in a single sentence as another piece of information is casually dropped into the narrative. This is a book of suspense but not of the obvious kind, the tension is palpable and illustrated by Catherine‚Äôs actions rather than internal monologues about how scared she is, as she turns from a capable and decisive documentary maker into a scared shadow as she wonders what will follow, how far is the author prepared to go to completely destroy her life? Should she take the ending as a warning, all of these thoughts push real life to the periphery as she valiantly tries to keep the secret under wraps.<br /><br />Readers that aren‚Äôt keen on protagonists they don‚Äôt like may well not enjoy this as much as I did but although many of the characters in this book behaved in a way I wouldn‚Äôt, at no point did their behaviour seem out of character, they were real people behaving in realistic ways albeit at the edge of their sanity at times and I was utterly convinced.<br /><br />I‚Äôd like to say an enormous thank you to the publishers Random House UK firstly for publishing this book, and secondly for allowing me the great pleasure of reading it. Disclaimer will be published on 9 April 2015 and it is a must for lovers of psychological thrillers.<br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8017171530762589785">Disclaimer was my first step into the entirely unventured-before world of fictitious psychlogical thrillers (for me). The story was absolutely stupefying. It was ugly, disgusting and it creeped me out in so many places that I almost felt sick. <br/>I still read it though, because it was all these nerve wracking elements that made me love this book because of how much I hated it too. <br/>The descriptions were extremely vivid; this work of fiction just about came to life before my eyes and well...it wasn't</span>
  <span id="freeText8017171530762589785" style="display:none">Disclaimer was my first step into the entirely unventured-before world of fictitious psychlogical thrillers (for me). The story was absolutely stupefying. It was ugly, disgusting and it creeped me out in so many places that I almost felt sick. <br />I still read it though, because it was all these nerve wracking elements that made me love this book because of how much I hated it too. <br />The descriptions were extremely vivid; this work of fiction just about came to life before my eyes and well...it wasn't the prettiest of sights. It was gross actually and very very scary. <br />The prose and language were brilliant and intriguing. The story was disturbing and disgusting and lived up to these qualities consistently; it was unique and basically showed how evil and ruthless the world can be, that nothing is controllable, and what happens in the the dark corners of our world, and how we owe up to it all ourselves; and all this people like me fail to acknowledge in the flow of daily life. This debut was certainly engrossing, riveting and unputdownable. I wouldn't want to reveal the story here but just a bit:<br />Catherine Ravenscroft leads a satisfactory life with her husband and son, when a mysterious book finds its way into her home and....It all about her. <br />Soon she finds herself abandoned by her loved ones in her own hell as she faces her gruesome past and its present consequences and must prepare for its future results. To what extent will she go to force her enemies into declaring that she had been innocent all along?<br />Age rating: 16+ (though I wanted to make it 20, then came down to 17, but this could be the minimum)</span>

    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=netgalley-arc">netgalley-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1168742275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13143176187828602724">This is Catherine's story. And if there is a moral to it, it is this: Don't make assumptions based on what you don't actually know.<br/><br/>Catherine, wife of Robert, and at times reluctant mother of Nick, carries a crippling secret from her past.<br/><br/>Stephen Brigstocke, husband of now deceased author Nancy, and father of Jonathon who died saving the life of Catherine's son, thinks he knows what that secret is, and thinks he owes it to both his late wife and son to make it public knowledge.<br/><br/>Catherine says she </span>
  <span id="freeText13143176187828602724" style="display:none">This is Catherine's story. And if there is a moral to it, it is this: Don't make assumptions based on what you don't actually know.<br /><br />Catherine, wife of Robert, and at times reluctant mother of Nick, carries a crippling secret from her past.<br /><br />Stephen Brigstocke, husband of now deceased author Nancy, and father of Jonathon who died saving the life of Catherine's son, thinks he knows what that secret is, and thinks he owes it to both his late wife and son to make it public knowledge.<br /><br />Catherine says she didn't know Jonathon prior to his saving her son's life, yet all the evidence points to this not being true.<br /><br />Was Jonathon, as everyone believes, Catherine's lover? Or did he play a far more sinister role in her life?<br /><br />I wanted to like this book, but it largely failed to hold my interest. I found my mind wandering as I read, and several times I physically got up and wandered off elsewhere mid-sentence. Having said that, there are some beautiful passages of writing, e.g. "...this house meet's Catherine's eye and calls to her, like the phlegmy growl of a homeless drunk...."<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley, Random House UK, Transworld Publishers and author Renee Knight for the gift of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1628230415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Bill Kupersmith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12460952-bill-kupersmith"><img alt="Bill Kupersmith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428792100p2/12460952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628230415?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Kupersmith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Kupersmith" href="/user/show/12460952-bill-kupersmith">Bill Kupersmith</a>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628230415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15409648638077773542">Some of my most trusted Goodreads friends gave high marks to Disclaimer & I truly was pleased when we chose it for the Kindle English Mystery group read for April. But tho‚Äô it held my attention to the very end, a sinking feeling kept growing that there would be no big twist - that the cliched ending I‚Äôd feared would turn out to be it. But an all too predictable backstory is not the book‚Äôs principal artistic flaw. Rather it‚Äôs the basic conception. Although Catherine Revenscroft‚Äôs secret involves </span>
  <span id="freeText15409648638077773542" style="display:none">Some of my most trusted Goodreads friends gave high marks to Disclaimer &amp; I truly was pleased when we chose it for the Kindle English Mystery group read for April. But tho‚Äô it held my attention to the very end, a sinking feeling kept growing that there would be no big twist - that the cliched ending I‚Äôd feared would turn out to be it. But an all too predictable backstory is not the book‚Äôs principal artistic flaw. Rather it‚Äôs the basic conception. Although Catherine Revenscroft‚Äôs secret involves a crime, this book hasn‚Äôt a mystery story plot; no puzzle to solve except a mess of Catherine‚Äôs own making. But Disclaimer fails too as a domestic drama, that kind where an indiscretion from a character‚Äôs past is unexpectedly revealed, threatening her marriage. Such stories need believable characters we care about &amp; identify with. Catherine reminded me of a Helen Fitzgerald main character, but without the endearing dottiness. Her husband Robert behaves abominably, &amp; falls easily for the villain‚Äôs design. But had he known what had happened from the beginning, he couldn‚Äôt have been fooled. Their son is a useless druggie layabout, but again had his mother been open, in a manner suitable to his age, about what had occurred, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(&amp; what we learn @ the end he‚Äôd witnessed as a child) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>perhaps he would have developed into a morally healthy adult.<br /><br />As for the villain, Stephen Brigstocke - he vies with the narrator of Graeme Cameron‚Äôs Normal &amp; Gramps in Kate Hamer‚Äôs The Girl in the Red Coat as the most odious piece of slime I have encountered in recent fiction (their Audible readers gave each of them voices that made my skin crawl). Although Stephen is presented as a senile helpless old idiot, we are expected to believe he is able to edit and self-publish a work of fiction &amp; create a fake Facebook page as a lure. Of course in this kind of book there‚Äôs always a convenient computer-knowledgeable acquaintance &amp; a teenaged boy to teach an old fossil the intricacies of computer publishing software, &amp; the internet &amp; social media. He is trying to avenge he death of his son Jon, who drowned on holiday in Spain rescuing Catherine‚Äôs little boy, tho‚Äô Stephen‚Äôs belief that Catherine should have gone in instead (she is a very poor swimmer) hardly seems adequate reason to ruin her life &amp; marriage, even for someone a cucumber sandwich or two short of a picnic.<br /><br />This book is not a total waste of time. Morally &amp; spiritually &amp; artistically we can learn from comparing Disclaimer with better books. Had honesty, integrity, and openness characterised Catherine &amp; Robert‚Äôs relationship, it would have been invulnerable to Stephen‚Äôs lunatic scheme. We discover that principle - that relationships demand absolute integrity - from the classics of crime fiction such as Nicholas Freeling‚Äôs Gun before Butter, Tana French‚Äôs The Likeness &amp; P. D. James‚Äôs Innocent Blood. Indeed, the parallels between Innocent Blood &amp; Disclaimer leap out @ you; both Scase &amp; Stephen are seeking to honour the memory of a deceased wife by getting vengeance on a woman they blame for the death of their child. Seriously, before she writes another book I‚Äôd suggest Ren√©e Knight sit down &amp; (re)read Innocent Blood &amp; think about how P. D. James might have handled the plot &amp; characters of Disclaimer. The difference is not in the ingredients, but in the chefs.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janet " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janet " href="/user/show/19512233-janet">Janet </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1255768671554561849">Thank you to the author, publisher and Netgalley for the much appreciated copy of the book.<br/><br/>This is a debut by Renee Knight, which I found to be an ok read. It's the story of Catherine, a tv documentary filmaker, who finds a book on her nightstand and starts to read. A few chapters in and she realises that the book is mirroring events from her past which she had painstakingly managed to bury a long time ago.<br/><br/>In comes Stephen, a retired teacher, who is the author of the book and seems hellbent on m</span>
  <span id="freeText1255768671554561849" style="display:none">Thank you to the author, publisher and Netgalley for the much appreciated copy of the book.<br /><br />This is a debut by Renee Knight, which I found to be an ok read. It's the story of Catherine, a tv documentary filmaker, who finds a book on her nightstand and starts to read. A few chapters in and she realises that the book is mirroring events from her past which she had painstakingly managed to bury a long time ago.<br /><br />In comes Stephen, a retired teacher, who is the author of the book and seems hellbent on making Catherine pay for the past. What follows is a story told from different points of views, each telling their own story from past and present.<br /><br />What I struggled with was the pace of the book, it's slow, too slow for me, so it took an awful long time to engage with, in fact I'm not convinced I ever did as the book took me over a week to read. Even though the book is working on the premise of what is the big secret that Catherine is hiding, I found I just wasn't that excited to get there. The characters work well enough with Catherine and Stephen being the main leads and their voices are heard well, but there just wasn't enough for me to keep me wanting to turn the page. It was unfortunately an easy enough book to put down and not rush back to, which is invariably what happened.<br /><br />It all concludes reasonably well enough and the secret, is, well, the secret but I came away feeling kind of relieved it was all over. It isn't a bad book and is written well enough it just didn't click with me but I'm sure it would with others.<br /><br />It's an ok book which is why I'm giving it two stars.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15429136600005621159">To be published in April 2015<br/><br/>Disclaimer starts with an interesting and rather unusual premise. A forty-something happily married woman, Catherine, finds a book in her house. She starts reading it and slowly begins to see that it is all about her and her secret past. The author is a retired teacher, who is on a mission to make Catherine pay for the past and to ruin her life. Catherine and the teacher, Stephen become obsessed with each other. What has Catherine been hiding?<br/><br/>The book was at its stro</span>
  <span id="freeText15429136600005621159" style="display:none">To be published in April 2015<br /><br />Disclaimer starts with an interesting and rather unusual premise. A forty-something happily married woman, Catherine, finds a book in her house. She starts reading it and slowly begins to see that it is all about her and her secret past. The author is a retired teacher, who is on a mission to make Catherine pay for the past and to ruin her life. Catherine and the teacher, Stephen become obsessed with each other. What has Catherine been hiding?<br /><br />The book was at its strongest when we heard from Stephen and could see how he has become a victim of hate and obsession. As a character, I felt I understood him and could sympathise with him much more than Catherine. I was impatient to see what the big secret was with Catherine and to make sense of her strange reactions. It was Stephen who kept me reading. I was willing Catherine to just talk to someone.<br /><br />My main fault with the book was the ultra slow pace initially and the time it took to actually find out what was in Stephen‚Äôs novel. I became impatient for things to come to ahead. Anyone who struggles with the first part should keep reading to see where it goes.<br /><br />It was very readable and thought-provoking. It is a poignant reminder of how secrets can be damaging. I thought it was a solid read and I am sure it will appeal to many fans of psychological thrillers out there.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Thanks to Netgalley and the publishers for my review copy.</span>

  <span id="freeText8432718402487865503" style="display:none">British scriptwriter <i>Renee Knight‚Äôs </i>cleverly crafted debut, <b>DISCLAIMER </b> is a twisted, dark and chilling psychological suspense which brings new meaning to ‚Äúred herring‚Äù and ‚Äúdomestic suburban noir.‚Äù <i>What an excellent cover depicting the true nature of the novel. </i><br /><br /><b>Let me start off by saying,</b> this is one addictive book which grabs your attention! The British narrators, <i>Michael Pennington and Laura Paton </i> deliver a suspenseful performance, setting the mysterious dark mood, perfectly. <br /><br /><b>Two families. Two sons. </b> Stephen, Nancy &amp; son, Jonathan. Robert, Katherine &amp; son, Nick. <br /><br />Let the sadistic evil games begin. Or should I say, cat and mouse? Truth or dare? Revenge. She sees a young man, a photographer. Over 20 years earlier in Spain, 19-year-old Jonathan drowns, while saving five year old, Nicholas. <br /><br /><b>Someone is out there; </b> Tormenting her? These secrets have the power to unravel their lives. <br /><br />Stephen is a creep. (An old crazy man), a former school teacher, a stalker, now widowed. A plan. </i><br /><br /><b>Told in alternating chapters</b> and voices, a slow burning tale which draws you into the web of deceit, when nothing is as it appears. Chilling, terrifying, disturbing, haunting. <br /><br /><i>dis¬∑claim¬∑er A statement that is meant to prevent an ‚Äúincorrect understanding‚Äù of something (such as a book, a movie, or an advertisement). </i><br /><br />While this may not be the best psychological thriller of the year; however, very worthy of 4 stars for capturing my attention for hours, a chilling debut.     </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632394143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15415973946547139334">4.5*<br/>*Read through Scribd Audio*<br/><br/>Catherine's life is turned upside down when she recognises herself in a book that was mysteriously sent to her. The book, 'The Perfect Stranger', chronicles a dark secret from her past, one that she wants to remain hidden.<br/><br/>Stephen is an elderly gentleman who seems to be hell bent on ruining Catherine's life, enacting revenge for a tragedy that happened many years ago. He's responsible for publishing the book but this is only part of his plan and he's going to ensure</span>
  <span id="freeText15415973946547139334" style="display:none">4.5*<br />*Read through Scribd Audio*<br /><br />Catherine's life is turned upside down when she recognises herself in a book that was mysteriously sent to her. The book, 'The Perfect Stranger', chronicles a dark secret from her past, one that she wants to remain hidden.<br /><br />Stephen is an elderly gentleman who seems to be hell bent on ruining Catherine's life, enacting revenge for a tragedy that happened many years ago. He's responsible for publishing the book but this is only part of his plan and he's going to ensure Catherine pays dearly for her past.<br /><br />This isn't the usual read I pick up but it was recommended by someone on GR, I'm very thankful for the rec as this was a highly enjoyable thriller that kept me guessing as to what Catherine's secret past really was. There are quite a few red herrings and I certainly didn't see things playing out as they did which made it all the better. No pretty ending here but one that I felt fit the story and was satisfying.<br /><br />The two narrators did a fantastic job in bringing the characters to life. Catherine is a successful career woman who is happily married to Robert. Her failings seem to be as a mother, a role that she has never felt at ease with. She is an engaging character and it was easy to feel invested in what would happen to her.<br /><br />The other narrator provided the voice of Stephen, he's out for vengeance over something he thinks Catherine did 20 years ago. At times it's really shocking to hear his hatred for Catherine especially when his plans to ruin her life take on more sinister tones. Whilst his actions are awful I still felt sorry for him, missing his dead wife and letting his grief turn to hatred.<br /><br />Each audio chapter was alternated between the two characters, this kept the pacing tight and it was all too easy to start the next chapter to get closer to the true details of the incident.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15415973946547139334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pCC5jsejjWa8RrHDWSKcGlVwK5b+CSK2ImtCJ0cjcHLGLgmYv39N9Ugw7kFBdvhl7dzKQct+bqqb0mnvses+lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YYnw3VcFg6wZLzzxSKFdaborC0z6VI++y590L7CbiGIDh0DLL9lDP+1ZY3NQ9TkWAofqm88jw6JyJl/nRlPGhA==')})
  }

Yet there are moments of exquisite tenderness in these troubled lives. Georgette, the transvestite who falls in love with a callous hoodlum; Tralala, the conniving prostitute who plumbs the depths of sexual degradation; and Harry, the strike leader who hides his true desires behind a boorish masculinity, are unforgettable creations. Last Exit to Brooklyn was banned by British courts in 1967, a decision that was reversed the following year with the help of a number of writers and critics including Anthony Burgess and Frank Kermode.\n\nHubert Selby, Jr. (1928-2004) was born in Brooklyn, New York. At the age of 15, he dropped out of school and went to sea with the merchant marines. While at sea he was diagnosed with lung disease. With no other way to make a living, he decided to try writing: \'I knew the alphabet. Maybe I could be a writer.\' In 1964 he completed his first book, Last Exit to Brooklyn, which has since become a cult classic. In 1966, it was the subject of an obscenity trial in the UK. His other books include The Room, The Demon, Requiem for a Dream, The Willow Tree and Waiting Period. In 2000, Requiem for a Dream was adapted into a film starring Jared Leto and Ellen Burstyn, and directed by Darren Aronofsky.\n\n\'Last Exit to Brooklyn will explode like a rusty hellish bombshell She has had TV and film scripts commissioned by the BBC, Channel Four and Capital Films. In April 2013 she graduated from the Faber Academy ‚ÄòWriting a Novel‚Äô course. She lives in London with her husband and two children. ~ <i>Transworld Publishers</i></span>
